Response\nto Input of Figure 130\n\n148\n149\n150\n151\n\nEPS-695\n\n\nPURPOSE\n\nThe purpose of the EPS Qualification Test Unit testing was\n\nto qualify the EPS for use in the \'Skylab\' program and to\n\ndemonstrate that the instrument would operate satisfactorily\n\nduring, and subsequent to, exposure to the environmental\n\nrequirements of the end item specification.\n\nPROCEDURE\n\nThe tests described in this report were conducted in accordance\n\nwith LEC document EPS-503, Qualification Test for Electron-\n\nProton Spectrometer, P/N SEC39106425-301, S/N 1001. All\n\ntesting was conducted with NASA QA and an LEC engineering\n\nrepresentative as witnesses.\n\nTo maintain the test schedule and utilize available test\n\nfacilities, the tests did not follow the sequence called for\n\nin EPS-530. The tests are reported in the sequence in which\n\nthey were run, which is also shown in the test summary sheets,\n\npages 30 and 31 of this report.\n\nACCEPTANCE TEST\n\nPrior to the start of the qualification testing, the EPS\n\nQualification Test Unit was subjected to acceptance testing\n\nin accordance with LEC document EPS-489. \n Data from this\n\ntesting is shown in the data sheets that form Appendix A\n\nof this report.\n\n\nEPS-695\n\n\nQUALIFICATION TEST\n\nFunctional Test\n\nAs the final functional test of the acceptance testing was\n\ncompleted less than one week prior to the start of the quali\xc2\xad\nfication testing, the functional test of EPS-530, para. 2.1\n\ndid not need to be performed.\n\nThermal/Vacuum Test\n\nOn the 21st January 1972, the EPS Qualification Test Unit and\n\nits associated Bench Test Equipment (BTE) were taken to\n\nBuilding 33, NASA/MSC. The test article was installed in\n\nthe test fixture in chamber \'N\' and the BTE connected as\n\nrequired by para. 2.2 of EPS-503. A functional test was\n\nperformed and the chamber door closed and sealed,\n\nAt 1:58 a.m. on 24 January, pump down of chamber \'N\' was\nstarted. At 3:18 a.m. the BTE was activated, and the EPS\nelectronics package and detector temperatures were monitored\nevery 30 minutes, as called for in the test procedures, using\nthe instruments built-in sensors for temperature measurement.\nTest mode 1 - cold, operating - and its accompanying functional\n\ntest was completed by 5:50 p.m. on 24 January, and the test\narticle was switched into test mode 2 - cold, standby. Test\nmode 2 was completed at 7:45 a.m. on 25 January and functional\ntest data was then taken. A loss of electrical power in\nBuilding 33 between 7:56 a.m. and 8:25 a.m. delayed the taking\nof the functional test data, but did not continue long enough\nto cause drastic change in the test items internal temperature,\nand the functional test data taken is considered valid.\n\nI\n\nEPS-695\n\n\nAt 9.15 a.m. on 25 January the chamber and test article were\n\nplaced into test mode 3 - hot, operating.\n\nAt 6:00 p.m. on\n\n\n25 January, this test case and its accompanying functional\n\ntest were completed.\n\nThe chamber conditions were then changed to test mode 4\n\n-\n\nhot,\n\nsurvival - and the \'electronics\' power and detector bias supply\nto the test article were turned off at the BTE.\n\nAt 7:45 a.m.\n\non 26 January this final test mode was completed and the return\nof the test chamber to ambient conditions was started, and by\n9:30 a.m. the post thermal/vacuum functional test data had been\n\n\ntaken.\n\nThe test article was then returned to LEC\'s Radiation Instru\xc2\xad\nmentation Department. Visual examination of the EPS revealed\n\nno damage that would prevent the instrument from meeting the\n\noperational requirements. No discrepancy reports were generated\n\nduring the period of the Thermal/Vacuum test. Data from this\n\ntest is included in the data sheets forming Appendix B of\n\nthis report. Temperature and power profiles for each test\n\nmode are given on pages 33 through 36.\n\nEMI Test\n\nOn 28 January 1972, the EPS Qualification Test Unit was taken\n\nto Building 14, NASA/MSC and accepted for electromagnetic\n\ncompatibility testing to EPS-503, para. 2.8. Storage in\n\nBuilding 14 over the weekend permitted immediate commencement\n\nof testing on 31 January.\n\nRadiated interference from the test instrument was evaluated\n\non 31 January, and all levels of irradience were shown to\n\nbe within specification.\n\n3\n\nEPS-695\n\n\nThe instrument\'s electromagnetic susceptibility was evaluated\n\non the 1st and 2nd of February. Although susceptibility was\n\nnoted between 200 - 450 MHz, the levels were 6 to 10 dB above\n\nthe specification levels, hence the instrument\'s performance\n\nwas considered to be within specification.\n\nThe test unit was then returned to LEC\'s Radiation Instru\xc2\xad\nmentation Department for functional test to EPS-503, para. 2.9.\n\nAcoustic Test\n\nOn 8 February 1972, the EPS Qualification Test Unit was taken\n\nto Building 49, NASA/MSC and accepted for acoustic qualifi\xc2\xad\ncation testing to EPS-503, para. 2.10. The test article was\n\nthen taken to Building 262, NASA/MSC and installed on the\n\ntest fixture. The test article and fixture was then suspended\n\ninside the reverberant chamber and the door closed.\n\nThe test article was then exposed to 80 seconds of acoustic\n\nnoise to the spectrum given in EPS-503, figure 6, followed\n\nimmediately by 10 seconds at an overall level 4 dB higher to\n\nsimulate transonic buffetting. It was then removed from the\n\ntest chamber.\n\nVisual examination of the unit showed no visible evidence of\n\ndamage or failure caused by this test, and the test unit was\n\nthen returned to Building 49. On the morning of 9 February\n\nthe test article was returned to LEC"s Radiation Instrumen\xc2\xad\ntation Department, where it was subjected to a functional\n\ntest as per EPS-503, para. 2.11.\n\n\n4\n\n\nEPS-695\n\n\nNo discrepancy reports were generated during the period of\n\nthe acoustic test or the subsequent functional test. Acoustic\n\ntest data is shown on pages 37 through 40 of this report,\n\nand data from the functional test is included in Appendix B.\n\nShock Test\n\nOn 9 February 1972, the test article was transported to\n\nBuilding 49, NASA/MSC and accepted for shock testing to\n\nEPS-503, para. 2.6. The unit was instrumented with accelero\xc2\xad\nmeters in accordance with TPS EPS-1204.\n\nThe test article was then mounted to the test fixture V6-I-lI6\n\nattached to the 310 slideplate. This shaker system had been\n\nset up to produce the shock response spectrum of EPS-503,\n\nfigure 4. After subjecting the test article to shock pulses\n\nin the +X and -X direction, it was removed from the test\n\nfixture and the fixture rotated 90 to orient it for the \'T\'\n\nThe test article was then reinstalled on the fixture\n\nand subjected to the same shock pulse in the +T and -T directions.\n\n\naxis.\n\nThe unit was again removed from the test fixture and the fixture\n\nwas removed from the slideplate and mounted on the 249 shaker.\n\nThe test item was reinstalled on the fixture and subjected\n\nto shock excitation in the +R and -R directions. it was\n\nthen removed from the fixture and replaced on its servicing\n\nstand and returned to LEC\'S Radiation Instrumentation Department.\n\nUpon receipt of the test article at LEC, it was subjected to the\n\nbench shock test called for in EPS-503, 2.6.19 through 2.6.21.\n\nUpon completion of this portion of the shock testing, the unit\n\nreceived a functional check-out as per EPS-503, para. 2.7.\n\n5\n\n\nEPS-695\n\n\nNo discrepancy reports were generated during the period of\n\nthe shock test or the subsequent functional check. Shock\n\ntest data is shown on pages 41 through 70, and data from\n\nthe functional test is included in Appendix B.\n\nVibration Test\n\nOn 10 February 1972, the Qualification Test Unit was taken\n\nto Building 49, NASA/MSC and accepted for vibration testing.\n\nThe test article was exposed to the \'X\' and \'T\' axis random\n\nand sinusoidal vibration of EPS-503, para. 2.4. At the end\n\nof this time it was returned to LEC\'s Radiation Instrumentation\n\nDepartment for functional testing to EPS-503, para. 2.5. The\n\ntest article completed this functional test satisfactorily.\n\nA discrepancy report (DR EPS-0087) was generated regarding\n\nthe \'O-ring\' seal on the underside of the mounting flange of\n\nthe EPS. Sections of this had become unbonded during the\n\nconstant removal from servicing stand to test fixture and\n\nback. It was determined that this discrepancy was due to\n\nhandling damage caused primarily by the large amount of\n\nhandling required to do the testing and attempts to align\n\nthe hold-down holes with those on the fixture with the full\n\nweight of the package bearing down on the \'O-ring\' seal.\n\nThe seal was rebonded to the flange.\n\nOn 15 February, the test article was returned to Building 49\n\nto be subjected to \'R\' axis vibration. Due to the inability\n\nof the 249 shaker system to attain the levels required when\n\nthe spectrum was run as a single segment, the test spectrum\n\nwas broken down into 6 segments as shown in Figure 54, page 71.\n\n6\n\n\nEPS-695\n\n\nEach segment was run for 80 seconds at the nominal level plus\n\n10 seconds at the high energy level. Each segment of the\n\nspectrum is shown-in Figures 75 through 154.\n\nUpon completion of the \'R\' axis vibration testing (random and\nsinusoidal) , the test article was returned to LEC\'s Radiation\nInstrumentation Department for functional testing. The unit\nsatisfactorily completed the functional test with no dis\xc2\xad\ncrepancies in the data, and visual inspection of the unit\n\nrevealed no damage that would prevent it from meeting the\n\noperational requirements.\n\nData from the functional tests associated with the vibration\n\ntesting is included in Appendix B.\n\nHumidity Test\n\nOn 18 February 1972 the Qualification Test Unit was transported\n\nto Building 15, NASA/MSC and accepted for humidity testing.\n\nThe test article was placed in the humidity chamber and the\n\ndoor closed and sealed. It was then exposed to the humidity\n\ncycling described in EPS-503, para. 7.0. On 23 February\n\nthe unit was removed from the humidity chamber.\n\nVisual inspection disclosed some staining of a screw and\n\nwasher, also of the test stand, and some \'bubbling\' of paint\n\nwhere moisture had penetrated under the paint surface.\n\nDR EPS-0089 was generated at this time.\n\n\n7\n\n\nEPS-695\n\n\nThe unit was then returned to LEC\'s Radiation Instrumentation\n\nDepartment.\nThe outside surfaces of the instrument were wiped\ndry and it was allowed to dry out at room ambient conditions\nfor 8 hours. It was then subjected to the functional check\ncalled for in EPS-503, para. 2.13. During this functional\n\ntest, some data was not within the specified limits and\n\nDR EPS-0090 was generated.\n\nThe test article was then placed in a vacuum chamber over\xc2\xad\nnight, and the functional check repeated. The instrument\n\nsatisfactorily completed this functional check. Data from\n\nthe two functional checks is included in Appendix B.\n\n\n8\n\n\n13\'~444\n\nVI\n\nX,\n\nNASA\ng-71-41256\n\n4.\n\na\n\n44\nF,\n\nPhS\n\n4i\n\nko\n\n4\n\n4Vi,\n\niAr\n\n7-4\n\n4144\n\np2\'\n\nIN\'\n\n4\n\n\'\n\n4\n\n~4\n\n~4\nV\n\n\'J.\n\n$44~~~~~\n\n......\n\niJ0\n\n44\'\n\n<\n\n\'\'\n\n4\n\nt\n\nit,\n\n4\n\n4\n\n4\n\n\'\'\n\n44446\n\n4\n\n\'$4\n\n~\n44\n\n;4Y\n\nm\n\n4\n\nIf\'4\n\nI\n\n,\n\nI\n\n(D\n\nAp\n\nNASA\n\n-7777r\n\n-\n\nM~\n\n\xc2\xad\n\np\n\nCt\n\nH\n\nX\n\nH\'\n\n~P\n\nii-\n\nA-I\n\n\nK\n\nNASA\n\n________\n\n~\n\nS-71-41258\n\n"\n\n*\n\n4\n\nL\n\n\n/\n\nr\xc2\xad4\n\n*\n\n4\n\n444\n\nK\n\n,~\n\n44\n\n~\n\nK\nc<~\\jit~\n\n444\n\n4\n\n444~\n\nc$\n4\n4\n\n44\n\n<\n\n44\n\n-\n\n44\n\n-\n\n44444\n\n\'4\n\n~\n\n><44\'4~4\n\n44\n\n*t4\n4\n\n<\n\n4444444444\n\n4\n\n. Shock,\n\n\n22\n\n\n4I\n\nEPS-695\n\n\nThe temperature results from the qualification test agree\n\nclosely with those from the Engineering Test Unit test? and\n\nshow that the operating temperatures for hot or cold orbits\n\nare satisfactory and do not exceed the predicted values.\n\nFor test case 4, survival in \'hot\' orbit, which is not con\xc2\xad\nsidered an operational requirement, the test results are\n\nacceptably below the survival limits placed on the instrument.\n\nThe results of the functional tests (Appendix B) show no\n\nchange in the test unit\'s operating characteristics either\n\nduring or after thermal/vacuum testing, and the test is\n\nconsidered to verify the ability of the EPS to satisfactorily\n\nmeet its performance requirements in the thermal/vacuum\n\nenvironment.\n\nEMI Test\n\nThe test article was tested to NASA EMC-P-EB8-003.\n\nA\n\n\nreport on this testing was generated (EMC-R-EBS-003) and\n\nis included as Appendix D of this report. The instrument\n\nis considered to have satisfactorily demonstrated its\n\nability to meet the specification requirements placed upon\n\nit.\n\nAcoustic Test\n\nPhotographs of the test setup are shown in Figures 6 to 8.\n\nFigures 20 and 21 show the spectrum shaped for the \'maximum\n\naerodynamic pressure\' run. Figure 22 shows the spectrum\n\nshaped for the transonic buffetting. Figure 23 shows the\n\ndata taken during the actual I maximum aerodynamic pressure\'\n\ntest run.\n\n\n24\n\n\nEPS-695\n\n\nSubsequent to the acoustic exposure, visual examination of\n\nthe instrument revealed no surface or structural damage of\n\nany kind attributable to the test environment. The post\n\nacoustic functional test results show no change in the instru\xc2\xad\nment\'s operating characteristics, and the test verifies\n\nthe ability of the EPS to satisfactorily meet its opera\xc2\xad\ntional and performance requirements after exposure to the\n\nacoustic environment.\n\nShock Test\n\nAccelerometers were mounted to the test article prior to the\n\ncommencement of the shock testing, and Figure 13 shows the\n\nlocation of these accelerometers. Their purpose was\n\nprimarily to monitor the response of the instrument to\n\nthe increased \'R\' axis random vibration levels, however, by\n\nplacing them on the instrument at this point in time allowed\n\nthe monitoring of the shock responses of the unit also.\n\nThese responses were recorded and included in this report\n\nas follows:\n\nFigure\n\nDirection\n\n24 to 28\n\nAxis\n\n29 to 33\n34 to 38\n39 to 43\n\n+X\n-X\n-T\n+T\n\n44 to 48\n\n+R Axis\n\n49 to 53\n\n-R Axis\n\n25\n\n\nAxis\nAxis\nAxis\n\nEPS-695\n\n\nExamination of the input shock response spectra shows that\n\nthey are all outside of the test specification in a number\n\nof areas. All of the input spectra are above the test\n\nspecification up to 100 - 120 Hz frequency, with the +R\n\naxis being also over in the ranges of 1500 - 2000 Hz and\n\n3000 - 3700 Hz. The -R axis is above the test criteria in\n\nthe range 3100 - 3700 Hz.\n\n\nThe test inputs are below the test criteria in the following\n\nareas:\n\n+X axis\n\n430 -\n\n-X\n\naxis\n\n430 - 2100 Hz, 4000 - 5500 Hz\n\n-T axis\n\n850 - 2700 Hz, 3400 - 6200 Hz\n\n+T axis\n\n430 -\n\n+R axis\n\n400 - 1200 Hz\n\n\n-R axis\n\n450 - 1400 Hz\n\n\n750 Hz,\n\n750 Hz,\n\n850 - 1900 Hz, 4000 - 6000 Hz\n\n900 - 2700 Hz, 3300 - 6800 Hz\n\nHowever, it is felt that these input response spectra repre\xc2\xad\nsent as good a test input as could be achieved with the\n\nequipment available to perform this test in Building 49.\n\nStudying the responses of the vibration isolated electronics\n\npackage to the input shocks shows a considerable amount of\n\nisolation of the input, particularly when compared with the\n\nresponse measured on the baseplate accelerometer, which\n\nis not isolated from the input.\n\nVisual examination of the test article indicated no damage\n\nor failure that would prevent the unit from meeting its\n\nperformance or operational requirements. The unit was again\n\nvisually examined after the bench drop test, with the same\n\nresult.\n\n26\n\n\nEPS-695\n\n\nThe post shock functional check disclosed no changes in the\n\ninstrument\'s operating characteristics, and the test is\n\nconsidered to verify the ability of the EPS to satisfactorily\n\nmeet itr operational and performance requirements after\n\nexposure to the shock environment.\n\nVibration Test\n\nThe accelerometers attached to the instrument prior to the\n\nshock test were used to monitor the responses of the instru\xc2\xad\nment to random vibration inputs. Responses to sinusoidal\n\nvibration input were not recorded. Though required\n\nprimarily to monitor responses to increased \'R\' axis\n\nvibration levels, the accelerometers were also used to\n\nrecord the \'X\' and \'T\' axis responses.\n\nAs noted under QUALIFICATION TEST, Vibration Test, the\n\n\'XI and IT\' axes were run first, followed by a functional\n\ncheck. The input and response data for the \'X\' axis is\n\ngiven in Figures 55 to 64, dnd for the IT\' axis in\n\nFigures 65 to 74. Data from the functional test is\n\nincluded in Appendix B.\n\nVisual inspection of the test article after the vibration\n\nled to the generation of DR EPS-0087 regarding the \'O-ring\'\n\nseal. It was considered that the cause of the seal coming\n\nloose was due to heavy handling rather than the testing,\n\nand the seal was rebonded to the mounting flange of the\n\ninstrument. No other evidence of damage that would affect\n\nperformance or operation was found. The functional check\n\nshowed no change in the data or the instrument\'s operating\n\ncharacteristics.\n\n27\n\n\nAs mentioned earlier, the \'R\' axis random vibration was run\n\nThe input spectra and response\n\nin 6 segments (Figure 54).\ndata from the instrument are shown in Figures 75 through 134.\n\nVisual examination of the instrument after the \'R\' axis\n\nvibration revealed no evidence of damage that would affect\n\nperformance or operation of the instrument. The functional\n\ntest disclosed no change in data or operating characteristics\n\nof the EPS. Data from this functional test appears in\n\nAppendix B.\n\nHumidity Test\n\nVisual examination of the test article after completion of\n\nthe humidity cycling disclosed some tstaining\' of a screw\n\nand washer used to mount the top plate of the instrument\n\nto the top slice of the electronics package, and some small\n\nareas of thermal control paint were \'bubbled\' where moisture\n\nhad penetrated under the paint skin. These flaws are\n\nmentioned in DR EPS-0089 which was generated at this time.\n\nDuring the functional test, certain data was out of\n\nspecification.\n\ne Medium voltage ADC, 1.0, 2.0, 3.0, 4.0 and 4.9 Vdc\n\ninput voltage: output voltage checked low.\n\n" Discriminator reference monitor checked 2.965 Vdc\n\nshould be 3.0 \xc2\xb1 .02 Vdc.\n\n\n28\n\n\n.EPS-695\n\n\nDR EPS-0090 was generated to cover these discrepancies.\n\nThe\n\n\ntest unit was placed in a vacuum of 70 microns or lower and\n\nallowed to remain overnight. The functional check was then\n\nrepeated and all data was found to be within specification.\n\nData from the initial functional check is included in\n\nAppendix B, and from the final checkout is included on the\n\nDR (see Appendix E of this report).\n\nThe \'staining\' of the screw and washer and the bubbling of\n\nthe paint were not considered to be problems that would\n\naffect the operational or performance characteristics of\n\nthe instrument. The out of tolerance condition noted during\n\nthe functional test was demonstrated to return to an in\xc2\xad\ntolerance condition as the instrument dried out. It is\n\ntherefore considered that the test verified the ability of\n\nthe EPS to satisfactorily operate in a space environment\n\nafter being subjected to humidity.\n\n\n29\n\n\nTEST SUMMARY SHEET\n\nEPS QUALIFICATION TEST UNIT \n\nITEM:\nPART NO.: SEC39106425-301\nSER. PROCEDURE\n\n1.\n1.1\n\nOBJECTIVES AND REQUIREMENTS\n\nOBJECTIVE\n\n\nThe objective of this test is to verify the operational\n\nintegrity of the Electran-Proton Spectrometer--(EPS).\nThe\ntest will be conducted on the completed EPS, therefore, the\n\nacceptance tests,\n\n(EPS Acceptance Test Procedure, LEC\n\n\nDocument A EPS-489) will be conducted on the EPS prior to\n\nthe start of this test.\n\n1.2\n\nENVIRONAENTAL TEST REQUIREMENTS\n\nThe following environmental tests required by the End Item\nSpecification and the Interface Control Documents wiil be\nconducted at the various NASA/ISC test facilities in\n\naccordance with the EPS Contract NAS 9-11373. The tests\n\nwill be conducted in the sequence beiow, however, -tis is\n\nsubject to change should scheduling problems be encountered\nat MSC test facilities.\n\nWhen specified, visual inspection\n\nwill be performed between the following tests.\n\nTest Sequence\n\nTest Type\n\n\n1\n\nFunctional\n\n\n2\n\nThermal Vacuum\n\n\n3\n4\n\nVibration\nShock\n\n\n5\n\nEMC\n\n\n6\n7\n\nAcoustic\n\nHumidity\n\nEPS-503\n\n\nTests to determine that the EPS is operating within specifi\xc2\xad\ncation tolerances will be conducted during the Thermal\n\nVacuum and EMC tests and before and after for all other tests.\n\nThe EPS electronics will be calibrated prior to conducting\n\nthis test and no adjustments or tuning of the EPS will be\n\npermitted during the testing.\n\nEach of the EPS systems including the scientific analog\n\nsystem, power system, temperature control system, housekeeping\n\nsystem, and the data processor system will be thoroughly\n\nexercised during the test.\n\nThe Bench Test Equipment (BTE) will be utilized during the\n\ntest to provide power, timing signals, and test input signals,\n\nand to process data from the EPS by providing data storage,\n\ndata decompression, engineering unit conversion visual\n\ndisplay, and hard copy print out of all data. The BTE\n\nprovides an interface to the EPS equivalent to that provided\n\nby the spacecraft/telemetry system in that it provides the\n\nsame timing, voltage and impedance levels, signal rise times\n\nand power as does the spacecraft interface/telemetry system.\n\n1.3\n1.\n\nEQUIPMENT REQUIRED\n\nFunctional:\n\n\nBTE (including test cables)\n\n(39106424)\n\n\nPower Design 2005 Power Supply S/N\n\n2\n\n\n7 3/3\n\n\nEPS-503\n\n\n2.\n\nThermal Vacuum\n\nThermal/Vacuum Chamber (Chamber \'N\') \t\n\nj\n\nTest Fixture. \n\n\n3.\n\n(\n\n/V Facility\nBldg. 33,\nNTASA/,1SC\n\n\nVibration\n\n\nGVL Control System\n\n249 Shaker\n\nVibration Facility\n\n\nDual 310 Slideplate\nFixture V6-1-116\n\n\nBldg. 49, NASA/MSC\n\n\n4.\n\nShock\n\n\nGVL Control System\nFixture V6-1-116\n\nVibration Facility\n\nBldg. 49, NASA/SC\n\n\nStand SEC39107541\n\n5.\n\nEMC\n\n\nStand SEC39107541 \t\n\n6.\n\nTest Facility\n\nBldg. 14, NASA/MSC\n\n\nAcoustic\n\n\nReverberent \t Chambers\n\nTest Facility\nBldg. 262, NASA/MSC\n\n7.\n\nHumidity\n\nHumidity-Temperature Chamber\nand associated equipment\n\n)\n/\n\nHumidity Test Connector\n\nSEC39107561-301\n\nStand SEC39107541.\n\n\n-3\n\nTest Facility\nBldg. 15, NASA/MSC\n\nEPS-503\nRevised 2-8-72\n\n\n1.4\n1.\n\nTEST ENVIRONMENT AND SPECIFICATION\n\nFunctional\n\n\nPrior to any environmental test, and subsequent to the\n\ntest articles exposure to that environment, a functional\n\ntest shall be run to ascertain that the test article is\n\noperational.\n\nIf less than one week has elapsed since the last functional\n\ntest was conducted after an environmental exposure, that\n\ntest may serve as verification of proper performance before\n\nsucceeding environmental exposure.\n\n2.\n\nThermal Vacuun\n\n\nt\nThe following \test cases will be conducted,\n(a)\n\noperating - (NR Document M104-02120\xc2\xad\n\n(b)\n\nMIL 7 STD-810B, Method 516.1, Procedure V.\n\nTest (a) consists of subjecting the test artrcle to a pulse\n\nthat produces the shock spectrum shown in Figure 4. The\n\ntest article shall be subjected to this pulse once in each\n\ndirection for the three mutually perpendicular axes (total\n\nof 6 shocks).\n\nTest (b) consists of placing the test article, in its assembly\n\nand servicing stand, on a wooden bench top at least 1 5/8"\n\nthick and performing the following:\n\nWith the stand resting on its base lift one edge of the base\n\nfour inches and allow the unit to drop back freely to the\n\nhorizontal bench top. Repeat using the other three edges\n\nas pivot points for a total of four drops. Functionally\n\ntest unit and compare with previous test results. Figure 5\n\nshows test arrangement for Procedure V.\n\n5.\n\nEMC\n\n\nThe EMC test will be conducted in accordance with Qualifi\xc2\xad\ncation Procedure for Electromagnetic Interference and\n\nSusceptibility Tests, Skylab Electron-Proton Spectrometer,\n\nEMC-P-EBS-003, and North American Rockwell !CD\n\nM 104-02057-234.\n\n\nEPS-503\n\n\n6.\n\nAcoustic\n\n\nThe acoustic test\n\nshall be run in\n\naccordance with MIL-STD\xc2\xad\n\n810B, Method 515, Procedure I with the following exceptions:\n\n\n(a)\n\nThe sound pressure ievels shall be as shown in Figure 6\n\n(b)\n\nThe test time shall be 80 seconds of nominal exposure\n\n+ 10 seconds of exposure -to the \'transonicbiuffeting levels.\nThese test levels shall apply to the top (detector) face of\nthe instrument. The sides of the instrument will be exposed\n\nto a level approximately 6 dB lower, when mounted on the\ntest fixture.\n\nAt the conclusion the unit shall be functionall\n\n\ntested and the results compared with previous functional test\n\nresults.\n\n7.\n\nHumidity\n\n\nThe humidity test will be run to MIL-STD-810B. Method 507,\n\nProcedure 1, except that the minimum temperature shall be\n\n680 F and the maximum temperature shall be 1201F.\nshall be repeated for five cycles only.\n\n\nThis test\n\n\nIn general Procedure I consists of exposing the unit under\n\ntest to the following conditions.\n\n(a)\n\nRaise temperature from ambient to 1200F and humidity\n\n\nto 95% over a two hour period.\nfor six hours.\n\n\nMaintain this condition\n\n\nEPS-503\n\n\n(b)\n\nOver a period of 16 hours reduce temperature to 68\'F\n\nand 850 or greater relative.humidity.\n(c)\n\nRepeat steps (a) and (b) for 5 cycles (120 hours).\n\n(d) Allow the EPS to remain at room ambient conditions\n\nwith no power applied for-8 hours.\n(e)\n\nFunctionally operate test unit at ambient conditions\nand compare with previous results.\n1.5\n\nFAILURE REPORTS\n\n\nAll failures will be reported in compliance with paragraph\n\nA A A I nlZ\n\nugw-r).59..449\n\n9\n\n\nET\'S-503\n\n\n2.\n2.1\n\nTEST PROCEDURE\n\nFUNCTIONAL TEST\n\n\n2.1.1 \tTurn OFF all EPS power at the BTE.\n\n2.1.2 \t Connect the EPS_ to BTE as shown in Figure 7..\n2.1.3 \n Place the BTE output power voltage level selection\nswitch in the medium position.\n\n2.1.4 \t Turn the Heater Power Switch to ON and verify that the\nactual voltage.\n\noutput voltage is +27.5 \xc2\xb1 0.5 Vdc. \n Record \t\n2.1.5 \n Record the EPS Heater input current on the data sheet.\n\ncurrent is within the acceptance limits\n\nVerify that this \n\ngiven on the data sheet.\n\n2.1.6 \t Turn the Electronics Power Switch to ON and verify\n\nthat the output voltage is 27.5 \xc2\xb1 0.5 Vdc. \nRecord actual voltage.\n\n2.1.7 \t Record the EPS Electronics input- current on the data\n\nsheet. \n Verify that this current-is within the acceptance\n\ngiven on the data sheet.\n\nlimits \t\nCAUTION\n\nDo not apply Detector Bias when Detector PlateTemperature\n\nMonitor indicates 251C or higher. \n if Detector Plate Tempera-\n\nture reaches 25 0 C. remove Detector Bias if applied. QUALIFICATION\n\nTEST REPORBT\nMSC/TCSD DOCUMENT EMC-R-EBB-003\n\n\n1.0\n\nGENERAL\n\nThis document reports the results of Electromagnetic Interference and\nSusceptibility Qualification Tests performed on the Skylab Electron/\nProton Spectrometer, Serial Number 1001.\n\nTesting was begun on 31\n\n\nJanuary, 1972 and completed on 2 February, 1972.\n\nTests were performed\n\nin the MSC Building 14 Electromagnetic Interference Test Laboratory\nunder the direction of the Electromagnetic Systems Branch of the Telemetry\nand Communications Systems Division.\n\nThe tests were performed in\n\naccordance with the requirements of NR Specification MHOh-02057-23h\n\nand Interface Revision Notice 9395 as delineated in MSC/TCSD Document\n\nEMC-P-EBS-003.\n\n\n2.0\n\nTEST EQUIPMENT\nA list of the test equipment used in the performance of these tests\n\nis contained in Appendix A.\n\nReceiver noise level data for each RIFI\n\nmeter used in these tests are presented in Appendix C.\n\n3.0\n\nTEST PROCEDURE DEVIATIONS\nOne deviation to the procedures of M4C-P-EB8-0o3 (Appendix D) was\nrequired in the performance of this test.\n\nSkylab telemetry trans\xc2\xad\n\nmitters operating in the frequency range 230 to 250 MHz generate\nfields in excess of the IV/M radiated susceptibility field required\nby NR Specification M&104-62057-234 and IRN9395 it\n\nthis frequency range.\n\nIn order to insure the compatibility of the Spectrometer with these\ntransmitters, the test signal amplitude was increased to 7V/M.\n\nAn\n\napproved Test Procedure Deviation Sheet is contained in Appendix D.\n\n\nDate:\n\n7 February 1972\n\nNASA/MSC\nHouston, Texas\n\n4.o\n\nPage\n\n2\n\nof\n\n4\n\nDocument: EMC-R-EB8-OO3\n\n\nTEST RESULTS\nA photograph of the test setup is shown in Figure 1. The duct\n\nwork shown in the photograph is a part of the cooling scheme contrived\n\nto divert cool air from the shielded enclosure air conditioning\nsystem directly to the Spectrometer to prevent over heating.\ntest cables shown protruding from the top of the\n\nThe\n\n\nspectrometer were\xc2\xad\n\nused during pre and post-test checkout of the spectrometer and were\nremoved during Electromagnetic Interference and Susceptibility\nTesting.\n\nCompleted data sheets are contained in Appendix B. Texas\n\nSKYLAB ELECTRON/PROTON SPIECTROETER\nQUALIFICATION PROCEDURE FOR\nELECTROnI4GNETIC INTERFERENCE AND\nSUSCEPTIBILITYZ TESTS\n\n\n1.0\n\nGENEfRAL\n\nThis document establishes the procedures for electromagnetic\ninterference and susceptibility qualification testing of the\n\nSkylab Electron/Protron Spectrometer, hereinafter referred to as\nthe Spectrometer.\n\n\nThe purpose of these tests is to to determine if the levels of\n\ninterference emanating from the Spectrometer and the response of\n\nthe Spectrometer to externally generated electromagnetic inter\xc2\xad\nference are within established limits.\n\n\nThe tests will be performed in the electromagnetic compatibility\n\n(EMC)\n\ntest facilities located in Building 14 at the Manned\n\nSpacecraft Center under the direction of the Electromagnetic\n\nSystems Branch (ESB)\'of the Telemetry and Communications Systems\n\nDivision (TCSD).\n\n\n2.0\n\nQUALITY ASSURANCE REQUIREMENTS\n\n\nIt\n\nis\n\nimportant that each step in\n\nthe procedure be followed as\n\nsbown to permit satisfactory evaluation of the test results.\n\nWhere RECORD is indicated in the text, insert the values\n\nobtained for that measurement on the indicated data sheet.\neach step in its entirety prior to starting the test.\nall tests under the test conditions delineated in ICD\n234A as revised by 1) the\n\noutput of any of the\n\n6\n\nproton detectors and 5 electron detectors,\n\nas displayed on the B E Cathode Ray Tube, is equal to or exceeds\na count of 10, or 2) a loss of the sync word occurs as a-result\nof the presence of the susceptibility test signal.\n\nLoss of the\n\nsync word is characterized by a complete loss of output data.\n\n\n6.0\n\nTEST PROCEDURE\n\n6.1\n\nGeneral Requirements\n\n\nAll interferencertests shall be performed within the shielded\nenclosures located in the Building 14 EMC test facility.\n\nThe\n\npeak detector function of the interference measuring eouipmnent\nshall be used when scanning in search of frequencies of maxi=n=\n\ninterference.\n\nBroadband and pulsed cw interference shall be\n\n\nmeasured by using the equipment\'s peak detector function; nar\xc2\xad\nrowband (CW)\n\ninterferences shall be measured using the equip\xc2\xad\n\nment\'s average detector function.\n\nTransient interference shall\n\n\nbe measured using the peak detector and the aural slideback\n\ntechnique of measurement.\n\n\nAll interference measuring test equipment and general test support\n\nequipment shall be operated in accordance with the manufactuxer\'s\n\ninstruction manuals.\n\nOperating instructions for the Electron/\n\n\nProton Spectrometer Bench Test Equipment (BTE) shall be included\n\nin\n\nthe Test Preparation Sheet (TPS)\n\nauthorizing the test.\n\nThe procedure for determining measurement frequencies prescribed\nin paragraph 2 of MiSC-00168, Appendix A, will be utilized.\n\nDate:\n\nPage\n\nNASA/MBC\n\n6 October 1971\n\nof\n\n1!\n\nDocument: EMC-P-EB8-O03\n\nHouston, Texas\n\n6.2\n\n5\n\nTEST SETUP\n\nThe spectrometer shall be mounted on and bonded to the EM4I test\n\nfixture, which, in turn, shall be mounted on and bonded to the\n\nshielded enclosure ground plane.\n\nThe basic test setup for the\n\n\nspectrometer is shown in Figure A-2.\n\nThe Spectrometer pin\n\n\nfunctions and loading requirements for interference testing are\n\nshown in Figure A-3. During susceptibility testing, the Spectrom\n\neter BTE will replace the load box shown in Figures A-2 and A-3.\n\nThe BTE shall be located outside the shielded enclosure. The\n\nbasic test setup of Figure A-2 shall be modified as prescribed\n\nby the various test methods of mSC-00168 or Appendix B of this\n\ndocument.\n\nIn those cases where MSC-00168 requires use of Line\n\n\nImpedance Stabilization Networks (LISN), use Solar type\n\n6512-106R lO-ufd RF Capacitors instead of the LISN\'s. During\n\nall testing, except radiated interference testing, use the\n\nHP-6226A power supply.\n\nLocate it on the test bench with\n\n\n24 + I" leads between the power supply and the Spectrometer.\n\nFor radiated interference testing, the power supply shall be\n\nlocated external to the shielded enclosure.\n\n6.3\n\nTEST REQUIRENTS\nTables II and Ii\n\nlist the interference and susceptibility\n\n\ntests, respectively, to be performed on the Spectrometer. Spectrometer Cabling and Loading Requirements\n\n\nA-3\n\n\nAPPENDIX B\n\nSUPPLEMENTARY TEST METHODS\n\n\nSUPPLEW\n,iTARY\nTest Method 1:\n\nTEST MTHODS\n\n\nConducted Interference Using an Oscilloscope on.\n\n\nDC Input Power Leads\n\nThis test method is used to measure conducted interference voltages\n\nappearing on input power leads in the frequency range 0 to the\n\nOscilloscope bandwidth.\n\na. \t\nTest Setup:\n\nFigure B-1 shows a typical test setup for use with\n\n\nthis test method.\n\nThe power supply shall be located inside\n\n\nthe shielded enclosure for this test.\n\nThe lead length between\n\n\nthe test sample and the power supply, including the length of\n\nthe power line test standard, shall be as specified in the test\n\nprocedure. If flight cables are available, they will be used\n\ninstead of the power line test standard.\n\nBonding or grounding\n\n\nof the test sample and/or shields to the ground plane will be\n\nas specified in the test procedure. The third pin on the\n\noscilloscope power cord will be isolated from ground.\n\nb. \tTest Equipment: The following items of test equipment (or\n\nequivalents) are required to perform this test method.\n\n(1) Power supply meeting the impedance requirements of the\n\ngoverning EMI specification and capable of supplying the\n\npower requirements of the test sample.\n\n(2) \t\nPower line test standard conforming to the requirements\n\nof the governing EMI specification.\n\n\n(3) Oscilloscope with the bandwidth and sensitivity required\n\nby the governing EMI specification.\n\n\nB-I\n\n\nGround Plane\n\n\nLine Test Standard\n\n\nPowerPower\n\nVert.\n\nIGnd\n\n\nOscilloscope\n\n\nNotes:\n\n(i) Bond or ground test sample chassis, shields, and signal\n\nreturn as required in the test procedure.\n\n(2) Third pin on oscilloscope power cord is not grounded.\n\n\nFigure B-1.\n\nConducted Interference Using Oscilloscope on DC Power Lines\n\n\nMeasurement Procedure\n\nc. \t\n(1) Set up the equipment as shown in Figure B-I.\n\nThe\n\n\noscilloscope probe is connected to the power leads as\n\nclose to the test sample power connector as is\n\npossible.\n\n(2) Energize the test sample and test equipment and allow\n\ntime for warmup. Adjust the oscilloscope vertical\n\nsensitivity and time base as required to measure the\n\npeak-to-peak voltage of the displayed composite signal\n\nwithout regard to frequency. The oscilloscope AC-DC\n\nswitch shall be in the AC position. RECORD the peak\xc2\xad\nto-peak voltage of the composite signal.\n\nData Sheet:\nd. \t\n\nFigure A-17 of MSC-00168 is a sample of a data\n\n\nsheet which is suitable for use with this test method.\n\nf2.0 \t\n\nTest Method 2:\n\nRF Conducted Susceptibility Using Injection\n\n\nCapacitors\n\nThis test method is intended to verify that the test sample is\n\nnot susceptible to radio-frequency interference on its power\n\nleads.\n\nFigure B-2 shows the typical test setup for use\n\nwith this method. The line stabilization capacitors are\n\n\nTest Setup:\na. \t\n\nremoved for this test.\n\nThe bonding and grounding of the test sample and/or cable\n\nshields shall be as delineated in the test procedure. and shields as-required by test procedure.\n\n(2) Third pin on signal generator, shall not be grounded.\n\n\nFigure B-2.\n\nRF Conducted Susceptibiliby Using Injection Capacitors\n\n\nthe test sample meas\xc2\xad\nUnless otherwise specified in the\n\n\nured on the VTVM).\n\t\n\ntest procedure, the test signal shall be amplitude\n\n\t\nmodulated 30 percent with either a 400 m z or 1000 Hz\n\nsine waw as specified in the test procedure.\n\n\t\nScan the- frequency range required by the test procedure\n\n(3) \t\n\nwhile maintaining the required output signal level,\n\nDuring the scan, monitor the test sample output for\n\nevidence of susceptibility.\n\nIf such evidence is\n\n\nobserved, RECORD the test sample response and decrease\n\nthe output level of the signal generator until the evi\xc2\xad\ndence of susceptibility is just removed.\n\nRECORD the\n\n\nfrequency and threshold ,level on the applicable data\n\nsheet.\n\nData Sheet:\nd. \t\n\nFigure A-18 of MC-OO168 is a sample of a data\n\n\nsheet vhich is suitable for use with this test method.\n\n\n3.0\n\nTest Method 3:\n\nRadiated Susceptibility - Conical Log-Spiral\n\n\nAntenna - Calibrated Field\n\n\na. \t\nTest Setup:\n\nThe typical test setup for this test method is\n\nThe LSC"s are used with this method\n\nshown in Figure B-3.\n\nand are mounted on and bonded to the ground plane.\n\nThe\n\npower line test standard is inserted in the circuit between\nthe LSC\'s and the test sample..\n\n-The bonding and grounding of\n\nthe test sample and/or cable shields shall -be as delineated\nin the test procedure.\n\nThe transmitting antenna is located\n\n1 meter away from the front surface of the test sample.\n\nThe\n\nseparation from the test sample is measured"from the mid-point\n\nB-6\n\n\nGround Plane\n\n\t\n\nTo Power Source\n\nPower Line Test Standard\nTo\nMonitoring\n\nLSC \t\n\nEquipment\n\n\n-4 \t\n\n1M\n\nTrans mittin\n--I~\n\neceiing)Antenn\nAntenna\n\nCal Position\' \t\n\nC\n\nRIFI test procedure\n\n\nFigure \t B-3.\n\nRadiated Susceptibility - Conical Log-Spiral Antenna\n\nB-7\n\n\nof the conical log spiral antenna.\n\nThe antenna shall be\n\n\npositioned 12 inches above the least 90 degrees and,\n\nwhen the transmitting antenna is rotated through this angle\n\n\t\n\'about its vertical axis, the\'longitudinal center lines and\n\nplanes of polarization of the antennas Turn the\n\ntransmitting antenna to the cal. position. Adjust the\n\npower level delivered to the transmitting antenna until\nf\nthe \t ield intensity measured at the receiving antenna is\n\n1 v/M unless otherwise specified by the test procedure.\n\nNote the power level indicated or, the power meter.\n(This calibration of the field will be performed once\nper octave over the frequency range of the test and each\n\ntime the signal generator, power amplifier, test antenna,\n\nor directiona! coupler is changed as the scan is.made\n\nover the required frequency range.)\n\n\n(3) \t Turn the transmitting antenna back to the test position.\nIncrease the power level to the transmitting antenna by\n\n3 dB as indicated on the power meter.\n\nB-9\n\n\nScan the frequency\n\nrange required by the test procedure while maintaining\nthis power level into the transmitting antenna.\n\nTest\n\nantennas, signal generators, directional couplers, arid\n\npower amplifiers will be changed as required during the\n\nscan so that the test frequencies remain within their\n\ndesign bandwidths.\n\nDuring the scan, monitor the output\n\n\nof the test sample for an undesired response.\n\n\n(4) \t At each frequency to hich the test sample exhibits\nsusceptibility, RECORD the test frequency and test\nsample response.\n\nDecrease the power delivered to the\n\ntest antenna until the power meter reads the same level\nnoted in step (2) and again RECORD the test sample\nresponse.\n\nDecrease the power level delivered to the\n\ntest antenna, until the test sample no longer exhibits\nthe undesired response.\n\nTurn the transmitting antenna\n\n\nto the CAL position and measure the field intensity at\n\nthe receiving antenna. RECORD this field intensity as\n\nthe threshold of susceptibility.\n\nd. \t\nData Sheet:\n\nFigure A-18 of msc-oo168 is an example of a data\n\n\nsheet which is acceptable for use with this test method.\n\nTest Method 4:\n\t\na. \t\nTest Setup:\n\nInduced Field Susceptibility - Equipment\n\nThe typical test setup for this method is shown\n\n\nin Figure B-4.\n\nThe LSC\'s are used with this test method and\n\n\nare mounted on and bonded to the ground plane.\n\nThe power\n\n\nline test standard is inserted in the circuit between the\n\nLSC\'s and the test sample. IE\n\no 2% lossof aroat\n\n.RG.2A/Et 3\n\n.......\xc2\xad\n.......\n\n.............. \n\n\nC \n\n\n.\n\n-ur\'\n\n-"\n\n\n28.\n2.\n\nCause of Failure/Analysis Results (Continued)\nThe small "blisters and evidence of corrosion on slice\n\nassemblies resulted from either (1) moisture behind\n\nthe gold plating (entering either thru a pinhole or\n\nother flaw in the plating) or (2) where the gold plating\n\nwas missing when the unit was received from NASA/MSC\n\nTSD. The finish of the slices is (1) zincate immersion\n\ncoating followed by (2) copper flash, (3) bright nickel\n\nusing sultamate process (.0002" thk.), and (4) a bright\n\ngold plate using Sal-Rex BDT-200 process type 1,\n\nGrade C, .00008" to .0001 thk. per MIL-G-45204. This\n\nfinish is required on the outside surfaces of the slices\n\nfor thermal control. Since the plating is a composite\n\nof four separate layers, it is difficult to establish any\n\nreason for the blistering other than the extremely thin\n\naold coating did have flaws which allowed moisture to enter.\n\n\npEV.I RLtASON FOR CHANGE\n\nDRAW1NG NO\n\nT\n"\'".,,*L\n\nCHANGE\n\nDRAWING\n\n18508\n.k,\'\nBFOECTy~\n\n=F4&\n\nOF EXISTINGO\n-rAS liREWORK \n\nRETURN TO\n\nOEO\nCIMS\n\nEI\n\n14ODEL\nCONDEMN\n\n-\n\n,\n\n--\n\n1\n\n\xc2\xad\n\n_\n\nUXAVA\n\n_\n\n\'\n\n\nEF\'"CTIVITY\n\nNC\n\n\xc2\xad\n\nHEET\n\nQ\n\n-tPTDAERLA\'\n\nN\' $ hew~tC i&\n\nI F"\n\n"C.-\',tttCLC,\nC ,p\\ZN,\n\nNOTICE\n\nWOAUH\n\nLL\n\n\nAL\n\n\nE__)L D\nSTOCK\nD Z SC P 1P T 10N OF CHANGE\n\n2m?,\xc2\xad\npcq MPJFCM4- F\\T \\W1h PAOWT7\\W\n/\\Pt~fCtAlMvaRL E\\L~M TC2 E7UOWC2\n5%4(,\n\n.S401\'.\n\n\'\nPART NU%\nkk1C\n\n\nuEiP\\7\ncTP~ Q ti) QX)\n\nQW\n\n<""<\n\nAEC~TO~_______J\ntIRIAL\n\nSP201I\n\nCA ON\n10\n\nICAGE\n\n\xc2\xa3,t\n\n'
